    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer17291487518321752939">Joseph Vaughan's life has been dogged by tragedy. Growing up in the 1950s, he was at the centre of series of killings of young girls in his small rural community. The girls were taken, assaulted and left horribly mutilated. Barely a teenager himself, Joseph becomes determined to try to protect his community and classmates from the predations of the killer. Despite banding </span>
  <span id="freeText17291487518321752939" style="display:none">Joseph Vaughan's life has been dogged by tragedy. Growing up in the 1950s, he was at the centre of series of killings of young girls in his small rural community. The girls were taken, assaulted and left horribly mutilated. Barely a teenager himself, Joseph becomes determined to try to protect his community and classmates from the predations of the killer. Despite banding together with his friends as ' The Guardians', he was powerless to prevent more murders - and no one was ever caught. Only after a full ten years did the nightmare end when the one of his neighbours is found hanging from a rope, with articles from the dead girls around him. Thankfully, the killings finally ceased. But the past won't stay buried - for it seems that the real murderer still lives and is killing again. And the secret of his identity lies in Joseph's own history...</span>
  <a data-text-id="17291487518321752939" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/40822719?book_show_action=true">Dec 24, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer40822719" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer904632143495420814">Finally! I have finished this book. I thought I never would. It's SOOO slow-moving, but the prose is just brilliant. It reads like an enchanting, on-going poem. Don't read it for the story, read it for the words, because the latter far surpasses the former. <br/>However it is a good story as well, slightly marred by the fact that there was no mystery in it for me as two of my relatives let slip the murderer's name in front of me before I started reading. People like that should be hanged. <br/>But even th</span>
  <span id="freeText904632143495420814" style="display:none">Finally! I have finished this book. I thought I never would. It's SOOO slow-moving, but the prose is just brilliant. It reads like an enchanting, on-going poem. Don't read it for the story, read it for the words, because the latter far surpasses the former. <br />However it is a good story as well, slightly marred by the fact that there was no mystery in it for me as two of my relatives let slip the murderer's name in front of me before I started reading. People like that should be hanged. <br />But even that didn't ruin it for me, because this isn't a plot-led book. The words take on a life of their own. Magic. </span>

<div id="review_318517224" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/318517224" />
    <a title="Geraldine O&#39;Hagan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5885436-geraldine-o-hagan"><img alt="Geraldine O&#39;Hagan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351847412p2/5885436.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/318517224?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Geraldine O&#39;Hagan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Geraldine O&#39;Hagan" href="/user/show/5885436-geraldine-o-hagan">Geraldine O&#39;Hagan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer318517224&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer318517224" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5386162093180851781">I have no idea why everyone likes this book so much, as it's clearly crap. Not only that, but it takes an unnecessarily long time about being crap.<br/><p>The protagonist, Joseph Vaughan, appears to be suffering from some type of Narcissistic Personality Disorder. Or at least that's the only explanation I can come up with for his turgid prose, literary pretensions and ability to focus the story resolutely on himself for a full 400 pages. The reader is told of roughly 30 murders (it's hard to be precise,</p></span>
  <span id="freeText5386162093180851781" style="display:none">I have no idea why everyone likes this book so much, as it's clearly crap. Not only that, but it takes an unnecessarily long time about being crap.<br /><p>The protagonist, Joseph Vaughan, appears to be suffering from some type of Narcissistic Personality Disorder. Or at least that's the only explanation I can come up with for his turgid prose, literary pretensions and ability to focus the story resolutely on himself for a full 400 pages. The reader is told of roughly 30 murders (it's hard to be precise, as the uniformity of victim and circumstance leaves little material with which to differentiate them), a series of tragic deaths, a false imprisonment, the destruction of at least two families and the tale of Joseph's mother's descent into madness. All of this is related exclusively and entirely as it directly personally affects Joseph. All the most memorable facts from a child's history of Early-Mid 20th Century USA are trotted out as a backdrop to the fascinating life and terrible suffering of our hero. Civil Rights protests and a Holocaust of which the characters are oddly well-informed at a very early stage serve as stage-dressing to Joseph's single-minded obsession with catching the man apparently responsible for the death of every female he has ever met. A constant stream of girls and women enter his life as combination muse/breeding instrument, and are summarily dispatched for increasingly spurious reasons. At no time do we get any inkling of what any of these characters think or feel. They are essentially just extra building-blocks in the ever-growing and incredibly boring wall of pain and suffering that makes up Joseph's life.<br /></p><p> To compound the all-round awfulness Joseph is that most horrifying of creatures, the protagonist-author. We are forced at regular intervals to read extracts of his turgid prose, as well as to hear the encouragements of all his friends, family and acquaintances as they eagerly await his production of the next Great American Novel. This confluence of the author’s and his protagonist’s narcissism results in several instances of such epic self-regard that I began to feel quite embarrassed to be privy to Ellory’s private ego-stroking.<br /></p><p>Meanwhile the story drags on, its twee faux-American language and bloated self-love dragging it down at every turn. Finally the author, having obviously decided that the length and pomposity of his work has now reached a sufficient level for it to be declared classic, hurriedly bashes out a nonsensical dénouement, before concluding with a pathetically self-regarding ending in which Joseph is lauded as a Great American writer, presumably meaning that all those women and girls didn’t suffer in vain, as they are immortalised as weeping ciphers whose cries of pain provided the chorus in the operatic melodrama that was the life of Joseph Vaughan. The end.<br /></p></span>
  <a data-text-id="5386162093180851781" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/71168471?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linda Parks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linda Parks" href="/user/show/2182552-linda-parks">Linda Parks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2182552-linda-parks?shelf=absolute-favorites">absolute-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer71168471" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15904353276631509817">How exactly does a person move beyond a childhood filled with death? Death that seems to take form and follow... yet stay in front all the while, taunting with it's ability to control the very life one tries to escape? <br/>This story begins in early 1900's with the death of a young boy's father - and what follows is a not so sweet serial killer mystery in surrounding Georgia country where everyone is suspect and one boy is destined to be haunted - if not hunted - forever. <br/>I'll admit, I do like for s</span>
  <span id="freeText15904353276631509817" style="display:none">How exactly does a person move beyond a childhood filled with death? Death that seems to take form and follow... yet stay in front all the while, taunting with it's ability to control the very life one tries to escape? <br />This story begins in early 1900's with the death of a young boy's father - and what follows is a not so sweet serial killer mystery in surrounding Georgia country where everyone is suspect and one boy is destined to be haunted - if not hunted - forever. <br />I'll admit, I do like for stories to move a bit faster than 'Angels' did, but the way this one was told totally captivated me. I was more than impressed with the brillant prose contained on it's pages and there was just enough mystery to keep me guessing most of the way. It was a good story - and the reminder of fashions and placement of historical facts thrown in here and there definitely made you feel as if you were in that era - looking through that young boy's eyes and feeling the harsh life that surrounded him and his townspeople. <br />The most striking thing about this book, to me, was the way in which it was written - even more than the story itself. The rough, painful - even the morbid scenes - were described in a beautiful fashion. One can only admire someone with such a way with words and want to receive that presentation. I most certainly will be looking for more stories from Ellory. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15904353276631509817" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_509135966" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/509135966" />
    <a title="Philip" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/784983-philip"><img alt="Philip" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1200401064p2/784983.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/509135966?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Philip" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Philip" href="/user/show/784983-philip">Philip</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer509135966" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9393932764299727455">I’ve been too busy to review the last few books I’ve read, but I want to make the effort and start again.<br/><br/>OK, so I picked this off the shelf mostly because of the title. It’s a nice, lyrical title and the backcopy said it was about a young group of boys who band together to discover who is killing little girls in their home town.<br/><br/>Sounds exciting, right?<br/><br/>I’m really torn about this book. On the one hand I think it’s really well written, even if the prose does get a little purple and overly descriptiv</span>
  <span id="freeText9393932764299727455" style="display:none">I’ve been too busy to review the last few books I’ve read, but I want to make the effort and start again.<br /><br />OK, so I picked this off the shelf mostly because of the title. It’s a nice, lyrical title and the backcopy said it was about a young group of boys who band together to discover who is killing little girls in their home town.<br /><br />Sounds exciting, right?<br /><br />I’m really torn about this book. On the one hand I think it’s really well written, even if the prose does get a little purple and overly descriptive at times – that’s just my personal taste, but the real failing is the plotting and storyline.<br /><br />Contrary to what the backcopy says, this book is NOT about a bunch of young boys trying to track a killer Famous Five style. The Guardians, as these boys call themselves, only meet twice and are caught and bawled out the second time by the local Sherriff, so they never meet again. That’s it. That’s the end of that storyline. What the backcopy would lead you to believe is the whole theme of the book is actually begun and ended in a few pages.<br /><br />So what happens the rest of the time? Well, that I think is the book’s biggest problem, our hero, Joseph Vaughan, for ninety-five percent of this book doesn’t do anything. He gets on with his life and has the same trials and tribulations (though a few more tragedies) as anyone while these murders continue in the background. He feels bad, but he doesn’t go out and seek the killer. He doesn’t do anything about it.<br /><br />**SPOILERS**<br /><br />There are also some huge plot holes in this book. Joseph is obsessed with these killings, but when his mother – who has had a breakdown – offers to tell him who did it, he walks out. I think he does that twice. Surely you would want to hear every theory, not matter who it came from. This seemed really stupid and out of character.<br /><br />Another thing that annoyed me is after a certain death in the book, there are only two people who could be the killer! And no one figures this out. It’s obvious!<br /><br />Joseph goes to jail at one point and I have many problems with this. Firstly, there are so many holes in the case it could strain vegetables. People must have been very unaware of their rights in the 50s because even I, with no legal training, could have got this case dismissed. As it is, Joseph is sent to jail for ten years, which I think only takes a chapter to get through and this does somewhat undermine just how long he is falsely imprisoned, until his case is reheard by the Supreme Court and his conviction overturned. I must also mention his idiot lawyer, who I would have fired ten minutes after meeting him. Again, were people really so unaware of their rights that they just took the first schmuck lawyer they were given?<br /><br />And finally the ending, which also seems rushed and gives no real explanation of why the killer did these unspeakable things to young girls. Who the killer is seems to be just put in for twist value and doesn’t really make any sense.<br /><br />A promising beginning, but an unsatisfactory middle and ending.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9393932764299727455" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText5868776377493562221" style="display:none">A book with a lot of promise that fails miserably. What captured my attention in the beginning was the prose style...it was very evocative but then it came to drown in its over reliance on similes...that repeat themselves over and over and over.<br />The story itself started good but became unendingly episodic and cliche. The serial killer narrative and coming of age narratives never gelled. Characterizations were a little interesting but this was lost in a story that went nowhere, I stopped reading when he met Brigid (I just could not take anymore), and a style that was too heavy and too loaded with similes...more interesting metaphors would have helped break it up some.<br />The slow pace would have been more interesting if the introspection went beyond the obvious...almost cliche in its nature.<br />It was a disappointing book because I had such high expectations after reading the first chapter...but it faded quickly after this.<br />Not recommended...but I did not hate it either....luke warm is my appraisal. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15254853957726964884">Read it and WEEP!!!!!!!!<br/>Maybe or maybe not physically, but sure enough you'll weep inside at Joseph Vaughan's life in Augusta Falls and beyond.<br/><br/>Such a damaging life, as fear and outrageous violence takes away a normal upbringing, surrounding him with the ghosts of lost children, forever haunting his nightmares, as this beautifully crafted novel progresses.<br/><br/>You find yourself not so much identifying with the various characters in Augusta Falls, as becoming one of the townsfolk yourself, sharing thei</span>
  <span id="freeText15254853957726964884" style="display:none">Read it and WEEP!!!!!!!!<br />Maybe or maybe not physically, but sure enough you'll weep inside at Joseph Vaughan's life in Augusta Falls and beyond.<br /><br />Such a damaging life, as fear and outrageous violence takes away a normal upbringing, surrounding him with the ghosts of lost children, forever haunting his nightmares, as this beautifully crafted novel progresses.<br /><br />You find yourself not so much identifying with the various characters in Augusta Falls, as becoming one of the townsfolk yourself, sharing their fears, understanding their bigotry, living their dramas, the despair, and the ignorance.<br /><br />After reading a hundred pages or so I felt like I'd read a complete book already, such was the skills of Ellory's decription and character building.<br /><br />Not so much a book, more a total experience.<br />Not so much a murder story, more a journey through one man's tormented soul.<br />Not so much a great book, more a memory that can never be eradicated.<br />It left me utterly gobsmacked.<br />I put the book down and just sat there stunned.</span>

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer863026024" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6077420559538551021">Here is a man with “a quiet belief in angels” a man who is both persistent and intrepid; I found this book hard to put down, a beautifully written book, the prose illuminating and the story startling. Never once was I tempted to skip the long passages so confidently written. The author writes an Incredible and disturbing account of the long, long hunt for a child killer, and in so doing relates the poignant, heart wrenching story of the boy who became that man. Brilliant.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

           <span class="uitext reviewText">Eveyone who loves a thriller</span></div>

    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Carrie by: </span>
      Roger Ellory

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer21019987" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6364389130818591110">When I first started reading R.J.Ellory’s, A Quiet Belief in Angels, I thought,<br/> <br/>"This is a con.....this can't be right.....this is a joke!"<br/> <br/>I was convinced I was reading the works of the Master, Steinbeck.<br/><br/>Right from the opening lines, Ellory had me drawn in, taken under the influence of, and then totally intoxicated by his verbal skills and mastery over phrase, paragraph and perfect prose.<br/><br/>‘Sat at my window, chin almost touching the sill, and looked out into the night. Sky as hard as flint, the s</span>
  <span id="freeText6364389130818591110" style="display:none">When I first started reading R.J.Ellory’s, A Quiet Belief in Angels, I thought,<br /> <br />"This is a con.....this can't be right.....this is a joke!"<br /> <br />I was convinced I was reading the works of the Master, Steinbeck.<br /><br />Right from the opening lines, Ellory had me drawn in, taken under the influence of, and then totally intoxicated by his verbal skills and mastery over phrase, paragraph and perfect prose.<br /><br />‘Sat at my window, chin almost touching the sill, and looked out into the night. Sky as hard as flint, the scudding clouds thin and fragile, like they’d disperse with nothing more than a fingersnap, but all of it beautiful in a broken-up, haphazard kind of way; the ghosts of day-clouds, backlit afterthoughts to remind you of morning. The morning gone, the morning on its way…which one it didn’t seem to matter. In the air the crisp snap of lodgepole pine and bitter juniper made the taste of breathing sour and electric.’<br /><br />Pure poetry! <br /><br />‘Tried not to think of my father, the sound of his voice, the smell of him – bitter apples, coal tar, sometimes cigars. I closed my mind down to nothing. Waited and watched, and then waited some more. Tried to breathe deep and even and slow. Tried to close out the sound of bugs and trees, of wind and the stream. Tried to hear other things. Things that came from darkness.’<br /><br />More impeccable prose!<br /><br />Added to his power over words, was R.J.’s inimitable expertise as a story teller. I read with eagerness and yet uneasiness, the unfolding of the heinous, extraordinary crimes that disturbed and haunted the ordinary, hard-working, everyday folk of Augusta Falls, Georgia; commencing in 1939. <br /><br />As I travelled with him, sometimes coaxed, sometimes running ahead, I couldn’t help but feel perturbed that the road in front might not be going the way in which I wanted to walk……at times, as a reluctant traveller, he forced me to tread the path that he had beaten out and I became timorous, totally disquieted that the destination we were heading for was not one I would choose to aim for; not a place I would seek to visit.<br /><br />R.J. Ellory forcibly delivers, he will not disappoint! <br /><br />He is a Writer to be reckoned with and bears a name that one day, I am confident, will be reckoned up amidst the All Time Greats!<br /><br />Are we sure he did not sit and learn at the foot of John Steinbeck? <br /><br /><br /><br />Carrie King <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6364389130818591110" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_382791054" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/382791054" />
    <a title="Joe Maguire" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4899452-joe-maguire"><img alt="Joe Maguire" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1461000775p2/4899452.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/382791054?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joe Maguire" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joe Maguire" href="/user/show/4899452-joe-maguire">Joe Maguire</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781405606141" href="/book/show/13031704-a-quiet-belief-in-angels">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4899452-joe-maguire?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer382791054" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10140267461274439724">This is a somewhat difficult review to begin as I have quite mixed feelings having just finished the book. My conclusion is probably best summarised by saying that I really enjoyed the novel and am glad to have read it, despite some flaws that became more evident as the story developed.<br/><br/>The prose was excellent, with some descriptive passages that are pure poetry. This rich prose became a little formulaic as the book went on, and there was a noticeable increase in repetition of similes later in th</span>
  <span id="freeText10140267461274439724" style="display:none">This is a somewhat difficult review to begin as I have quite mixed feelings having just finished the book. My conclusion is probably best summarised by saying that I really enjoyed the novel and am glad to have read it, despite some flaws that became more evident as the story developed.<br /><br />The prose was excellent, with some descriptive passages that are pure poetry. This rich prose became a little formulaic as the book went on, and there was a noticeable increase in repetition of similes later in the book that made me wonder if the author was simply rushing. The pace is quite slow but for me the writing style was able to carry this and I never found myself bored. In short, the prose is the best feature of this book, giving life to a plot and characters which otherwise might have seemed flat, and making this read worthwhile.<br /><br />The plot and characterisation were engaging and there were enough twists to keep me guessing to the end. Having reached the end however, there are some aspects that I find unsatisfying -- not enough explanation of the motives of the eventual child killer, some lack of clarity about why our protagonist first takes such an active role (responsibility?) for stopping the killings, some odd decisions and actions which are not explained within the plot. Similar to my feelings about the quality of prose, I also had the feeling that the plot quality suffered as the book went on, and that despite the length of the novel there were plot elements and characterisations later on which were rushed compared to those earlier in the book.<br /><br />As with 'A Simple Act Of Violence' which I also recently finished, Ellory has clearly put significant time and effort into researching the historical, geographical and political setting for this novel and that shines through as a positive for me in both works.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10140267461274439724" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_260905806" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/260905806" />
    <a title="Morticia Adams" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2623624-morticia-adams"><img alt="Morticia Adams" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1254079524p2/2623624.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/260905806?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Morticia Adams" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Morticia Adams" href="/user/show/2623624-morticia-adams">Morticia Adams</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer260905806" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9303820445685166191">This wouldn’t have been a bad crime thriller, had it not been ruined by the author’s apparent belief that he’s a much better writer than he actually is. He aims for the lyrical and poetic and falls flat because he doesn’t apparently understand the value of restraint or economy, and that constant repetition of an idea will diminish its impact. <br/><br/>I suspect that many editors today aren’t ruthless enough, and are too ready to swallow their authors’ self-hyping. A good editor might have suggested that </span>
  <span id="freeText9303820445685166191" style="display:none">This wouldn’t have been a bad crime thriller, had it not been ruined by the author’s apparent belief that he’s a much better writer than he actually is. He aims for the lyrical and poetic and falls flat because he doesn’t apparently understand the value of restraint or economy, and that constant repetition of an idea will diminish its impact. <br /><br />I suspect that many editors today aren’t ruthless enough, and are too ready to swallow their authors’ self-hyping. A good editor might have suggested that Mr Ellory put less effort into the elaboration of his style, and more into ironing out the flaws and implausibilities of his story. Of the latter there are unfortunately quite a few: no insight into the motives of the killer, no satisfactory explanation of the narrator’s obsession with and irrational feelings of responsibility for the murders; inadequate acknowledgement of the traumatic legacy a series of such horrific crimes would surely have had on a small town where nearly everyone knew each other. And too many anachronisms in the dialogue - “enough already”, “enjoy”, etc – that’s just lazy writing!<br /><br />Despite this, I really think that as a story-teller, he does have some talent: I read the book to the end because I was keen to see the resolution of the mystery, and the identity of the culprit. But as a writer, sadly, he doesn’t have a great deal to say. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9303820445685166191" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1086459597" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2229662604898813075">I do not have the right words to describe my absolute love of this amazing and wonderful book. It is simply stunning. I have not been able to put it down and just loved Joseph Calvin Vaughan: I just wanted to hug him and take away all his pain and the terrible tragedies that dogged his life from an early age. <br/><br/>I have read some amazing books this year and had just finished a terrific book before moving onto one of my favourite authors, R J Ellory and this heartbreaking novel.<br/><br/>All I can describe it </span>
  <span id="freeText2229662604898813075" style="display:none">I do not have the right words to describe my absolute love of this amazing and wonderful book. It is simply stunning. I have not been able to put it down and just loved Joseph Calvin Vaughan: I just wanted to hug him and take away all his pain and the terrible tragedies that dogged his life from an early age. <br /><br />I have read some amazing books this year and had just finished a terrific book before moving onto one of my favourite authors, R J Ellory and this heartbreaking novel.<br /><br />All I can describe it as is a little like Shawshank Redemption with all the heartache that book delivered. <br /><br />My only questions would include why the murderer killed his victims in the brutal fashion that he did? Had something happened in his past? - but that didn't spoil the plot for me and didn't detract from my joy of reading it.<br /><br />I would dearly love this to be made into a movie and I would be right at the front of the queue wanting to watch it.<br /><br />Simply amazing, beautifully written (as always) and addictive read. I will never forget this story - ever.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leslie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leslie" href="/user/show/11351200-leslie">Leslie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer624645872374135503">4* for this audiobook edition; 3½* for the book itself<br/><br/>Mark Bramhall's voice was excellent for this book. It intensified the brooding Southern atmosphere significantly for me! As for the story, this isn't the type of mystery I prefer but I found it well written and the perspective of a person living in a rural area in which a serial killer of young girls is operating was interesting.   <span id="freeText624645872374135503" style="display:none">4* for this audiobook edition; 3½* for the book itself<br /><br />Mark Bramhall's voice was excellent for this book. It intensified the brooding Southern atmosphere significantly for me! As for the story, this isn't the type of mystery I prefer but I found it well written and the perspective of a person living in a rural area in which a serial killer of young girls is operating was interesting. However, there were a few times when the first person narration by Joseph Vaughn described things he couldn't have known or seen or heard about later. Also, Vaughn's sense of responsibility or connection to the girls is not normal nor adequately explained. It is necessary for the way the author concluded the case &amp; the book but it didn't feel natural.</span>

<div id="review_621239684" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/621239684" />
    <a title="Crystal Craig" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4729956-crystal-craig"><img alt="Crystal Craig" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1511938091p2/4729956.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/621239684?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Crystal Craig" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Crystal Craig" href="/user/show/4729956-crystal-craig">Crystal Craig</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4729956-crystal-craig?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4729956-crystal-craig?shelf=owned-print">owned-print</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4729956-crystal-craig?shelf=recommended">recommended</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4729956-crystal-craig?shelf=sweeter-reads">sweeter-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer621239684" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15572204450718617003"><b>mysterious, well-written, why?</b><br/><br/>When I got to the half-way point reading, R.J. Ellory's, A QUIET BELIEF IN ANGELS, something tragic happened. My chaotic outside life, the life I live away from reading got in the way. Nothing irritates me more. I kept thinking about the book, wondering what sick SOB was killing young girls, but be darned if I could clear my head five minutes to read. Finally, after having to abandon the book for a week, I finished today (Thursday, June twelfth, 2014). <br/><br/>This is my fi</span>
  <span id="freeText15572204450718617003" style="display:none"><b>mysterious, well-written, why?</b><br /><br />When I got to the half-way point reading, R.J. Ellory's, A QUIET BELIEF IN ANGELS, something tragic happened. My chaotic outside life, the life I live away from reading got in the way. Nothing irritates me more. I kept thinking about the book, wondering what sick SOB was killing young girls, but be darned if I could clear my head five minutes to read. Finally, after having to abandon the book for a week, I finished today (Thursday, June twelfth, 2014). <br /><br />This is my first time reading the author. The book is a Buddy Read for June 2014 in my book club, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/104180-sweeter-reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Sweeter Reads</a>. I really enjoyed the story, especially the first half when main character, Joseph Calvin Vaughan is just a child of twelve-years-old. I often find children make the best narrators; they're humorous and innocent and I love how that comes out on a page.<br /><br /><i>"She was a sweet enough child I'm sure, but to a twelve-year-old boy a nine-year-old girl seems the worst kind of harpy. Her voice was shrill, like a rusted spike jabbing my ears, and though later she would mellow and soften, and in her own way become really quite sensitive and beautiful, at the time she was like bitter-tasting medicine for an illness long gone."</i><br />[page 27]<br /><br />I found myself chuckling at Joseph and his buddies when they formed, The Guardians, a neighbourhood watch. Like six young boys would be able to catch a killer. To me, it felt like The Hardy Boys meets Stand By Me.<br /><br /><i>"'My dad has a gun, you know,' Maurice Fricker said.<br />'Everybody's dad has a gun, Maurice,' Ronnie Duggan said. 'My dad stands out back in the yard and shoots stupid kids. Figure you better walk home a different way.'<br />'I'm serious,' Maurice said.<br />'I...I could get one too,' Michael said.<br />'Christ, no,' Daniel said. 'Give you a gun, hell, the way you fidget you'd kill everyone standing.'" </i><br />[page 111]<br /><br />I loved the small town feeling and the tidbits of World War II history. As you read further into the book, young Joseph Calvin Vaughan grows into a man with the most tragic life ever. I didn't enjoy the latter half of the book as much as I did the beginning. Honestly, I just wanted to know who the killer was. And, when it was all revealed and I closed the book, I had one big nagging question. Why? What drives a person to kill so many girls? and to do so in such a brutal fashion. I wanted a explanation, one wasn't given, so this book gets a four star rating rather than five. <br /><br />Overall, though, I recommend the book. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="15572204450718617003" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_74848946" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/74848946" />
    <a title="Dorie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1412216-dorie"><img alt="Dorie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500594279p2/1412216.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/74848946?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dorie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dorie" href="/user/show/1412216-dorie">Dorie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781590202500" href="/book/show/6481106-a-quiet-belief-in-angels">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1412216-dorie?shelf=crime-fiction">crime-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer74848946" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1920660524613395077">This book starts when Joseph Vaughan's father dies. Joseph is 12 and hopes that his father has become an angel. That year the first little girl in his community is murdered. The book follows Joseph's life as he is touched by the horror of Hitler's war in Europe and the more local horror of the murders of young girls.<br/><br/>I have to say the plot was nothing like I anticipated. From the book jacket you are given to believe that the first part of the book will be about Joseph's childhood and the local mu</span>
  <span id="freeText1920660524613395077" style="display:none">This book starts when Joseph Vaughan's father dies. Joseph is 12 and hopes that his father has become an angel. That year the first little girl in his community is murdered. The book follows Joseph's life as he is touched by the horror of Hitler's war in Europe and the more local horror of the murders of young girls.<br /><br />I have to say the plot was nothing like I anticipated. From the book jacket you are given to believe that the first part of the book will be about Joseph's childhood and the local murders. Then, 50 years after the killings cease, Joseph confronts his past. This is not accurate at all. The book follows all of Joseph's life linearly after the age of 12 years, with no break. Some years are admittedly summed up quickly, but the killings do not stop and Joseph is only about 40 at the end. <br /><br />The beginning was well written and pulls you immediately into the story and inside Joseph's mind and heart. Admittedly the middle of the book began to drag a little for me, but at one point about 3/4 through I could not stop reading and finished it in one sitting. The ending was thoroughly engrossing and I had to keep reading to find out who the killer was. Your mind cycles through multiple suspects before the ending. <br /><br />The weaknesses: I thought in the beginning Joseph was much too young to be thinking such deep and morose thoughts. And his later sexual affair with an older woman struck me as wrong on her end. The story itself was written very dark, with the characters acting and speaking a bit melodramatically. But overall a really good and engrossing story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1920660524613395077" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_118748744" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/118748744" />
    <a title="Rose☮️" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/278701-rose"><img alt="Rose☮️" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496848953p2/278701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/118748744?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rose☮️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rose☮️" href="/user/show/278701-rose">Rose☮️</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/278701-rose?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/278701-rose?shelf=serial-killers">serial-killers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/278701-rose?shelf=book-club">book-club</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer118748744" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8224466731396824185">This book is in a class all by itself. A mixture of horror, drama, romance, mystery; I just can't catergorize it. Ellory deserves to be among the great classic authors, the one who comes to mind is Steinbeck. <br/><br/>The story is told through the eyes of Joseph Vaughan, a Georgia boy who grows up among the shadows of a serial killer who rapes, tortures and then tears apart little girls. Yes, it's disturbing, yes, it's gruesome and dark, but it's told with such beauty that even the most darkest of scenes</span>
  <span id="freeText8224466731396824185" style="display:none">This book is in a class all by itself. A mixture of horror, drama, romance, mystery; I just can't catergorize it. Ellory deserves to be among the great classic authors, the one who comes to mind is Steinbeck. <br /><br />The story is told through the eyes of Joseph Vaughan, a Georgia boy who grows up among the shadows of a serial killer who rapes, tortures and then tears apart little girls. Yes, it's disturbing, yes, it's gruesome and dark, but it's told with such beauty that even the most darkest of scenes are elegantly delivered. It's so rich in it's telling that I found myself just lost in it reading lines over and over again.<br /><br />"The flowers I had brought and set against the headstone were battered into handfuls of waterlogged petals. I stayed there until my clothes were almost too heavy for me to stand, and I thought about my loss and I shed no tears. I believed the sky was crying for me."<br /><br />Just a nugget of our narrator who allows you in in such a way as to feel his lack of belonging anywhere in the world, his sense of unease and loneliness is so heartbreaking. This is not a story with joy or laughter. It' dark and bleak with a great whodunnit thrown it for suspense. I absolutely LOVE IT!!!! This is a book that will stay with you and haunt you.<br /><br />Follow Joseph and the hunt that takes over his whole life and fall in love with this extraordinary talent.<br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="8224466731396824185" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_122553364" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/122553364" />
    <a title="Wayne Wilson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2249988-wayne-wilson"><img alt="Wayne Wilson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1240501292p2/2249988.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/122553364?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wayne Wilson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wayne Wilson" href="/user/show/2249988-wayne-wilson">Wayne Wilson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer122553364" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6779416637461969437">Wow! This was totally unexpected. This felt like true literature. A very dark book. A murder mystery but not like any murder mystery book I have ever read. From the title I was sort of hoping or expecting super natural events but it was not that kind of book.<br/><br/>We start out with a young man whose father just passed away, I think he is the 4th grade. He has a great teacher who challenges him and she see's in Joe (our protagonist) a writer to be. Well Joe has a girl class mate who is brutally raped a</span>
  <span id="freeText6779416637461969437" style="display:none">Wow! This was totally unexpected. This felt like true literature. A very dark book. A murder mystery but not like any murder mystery book I have ever read. From the title I was sort of hoping or expecting super natural events but it was not that kind of book.<br /><br />We start out with a young man whose father just passed away, I think he is the 4th grade. He has a great teacher who challenges him and she see's in Joe (our protagonist) a writer to be. Well Joe has a girl class mate who is brutally raped and killed. This affects Joe deeply and he uses his writing to exercise the fear and pain he feels with her death.<br /><br />These deaths continue over time as little girls are killed all around Joe's town and surrounding areas. Joe and several of his male friends form a secret society devoted to protecting young girls, yet these little girls keep getting killed. Joe is a sensitive soul and he even comes across one of the little girls who was killed.<br /><br />The book takes us through Joe's life and the killings continue. He becomes a published writer but things go from bad to worse as people he loves die and are murdered. There are some great twists and it is a compelling read. It is very dark and the killings are gruesome. Mostly I am left in the end very sad for all that has happened to Joe and these little girls because of one terrible killer.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6779416637461969437" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7797598928248934827" style="display:none">This book was recommended to me by a friend and I'm SO glad I listened and read this one. This was such a good story I didn't want to quit reading it. Could one person's life be just one tragedy after another as in this story? Joseph Vaughan lives in a town where a serial killer is killing young girls and he becomes engrossed with wanting to find out who the murderer is. All the while, he seems to suffer so many losses in his own life. The writing in this book is beautiful. I never guessed who the protagonist was, until just a few pages before he was revealed, it was a big surprise. I highly recommend this book. Read it, you won't be sorry!</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer596039620" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18275101321530267162">A slow-paced crime novel set in rural Georgia before the First World War. Little girls are gruesomely murdered, impacting the life and future of Joseph Vaughan, precocious teenager. It is slow going. A better writer would have gotten away with it, but Ellory's prose is over-the-top and repetitive, trying too hard to be poignant and poetic. Joseph's obsession with the murders and subsequent navel gazing might have been interesting had there been som depth to it, but he remains a two-dimensional c</span>
  <span id="freeText18275101321530267162" style="display:none">A slow-paced crime novel set in rural Georgia before the First World War. Little girls are gruesomely murdered, impacting the life and future of Joseph Vaughan, precocious teenager. It is slow going. A better writer would have gotten away with it, but Ellory's prose is over-the-top and repetitive, trying too hard to be poignant and poetic. Joseph's obsession with the murders and subsequent navel gazing might have been interesting had there been som depth to it, but he remains a two-dimensional character and the endless dwelling grows infuriating after a few hundred pages. The novel tries to be something it is not, and would have been better off as a straight-forward crime story. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18275101321530267162" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_271701002" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/271701002" />
    <a title="Ian Mapp" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1598886-ian-mapp"><img alt="Ian Mapp" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1291393306p2/1598886.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/271701002?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ian Mapp" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ian Mapp" href="/user/show/1598886-ian-mapp">Ian Mapp</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1598886-ian-mapp?shelf=crime">crime</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer271701002&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer271701002" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10319563365363303276">After four disappointments, my faith in literatrure is fully restored.<br/><br/>This is an incredible story. Before reviewing - who have to read the bio of the author on his web site, where his sense of humour and world weariness is explained - never knew his father, mother died when he was young, grandparents died, jailed for scrumping (is this true).<br/><br/>The book is written by a brummie and set in america in the late 30s to 60s... telling Joseph Vaughn's story.<br/><br/>The style is my favorite - a couple of pages at </span>
  <span id="freeText10319563365363303276" style="display:none">After four disappointments, my faith in literatrure is fully restored.<br /><br />This is an incredible story. Before reviewing - who have to read the bio of the author on his web site, where his sense of humour and world weariness is explained - never knew his father, mother died when he was young, grandparents died, jailed for scrumping (is this true).<br /><br />The book is written by a brummie and set in america in the late 30s to 60s... telling Joseph Vaughn's story.<br /><br />The style is my favorite - a couple of pages at the present - where Jospeth has tracked down someone to New York - shots are fired and both men are down. The present is returned to in brief interludes as the story is told from the start.<br /><br />Childhood in a Gerogian farm community is ruined by the frequent murders of young girls. Josephs life is not easy, his father dies at a young age, he catches his mother inflagrante with a married neighbour and he discovers a mutilated body. This is all told with a grim world weariness.<br /><br />With his friends he forms the guardians but nothing much comes of this - he is warned off by the sheriff when they are out on maneouvers.<br /><br />The serial killer aspect is a little bit away from the story. As he is a child, its all about adult realtionships and growing up - and WW2 and politcial incidents are used as a barometer.<br /><br />His mother slips into madness, his mother lovers family are burnt out of their home (germanic tensions and accusations that no american could commit the crimes) and Joseph settles down with his former school teacher - who encouraged him to write.<br /><br />Tradegy is always at his shoulder and just when you think he is settled and a baby is on the way, they both die in a fall.<br /><br />The german neighbour apparently commits suicide and artefacts from the murders are found in his new house. This is half way through the book and you know that all is not as it seems...... you are waiting for the twist. For a while, i thought the murderer was Jospeh himself, as he is an author and tricks / authors mind sets are often referred to.<br /><br />He rebuilds again - moves away to NY - finds a group of bohemian friends and a new woman and again - just when you think he is finding happines - she is murdered in the same way as the girls - the past has come to find him.<br /><br />This time however, there is a twist. At this point, I could hardly bare to read the book and wanted to cover the text further down the page so that I wouldnt accidently see what was going to happen. This is thriller writing of the highest order - no book has done this to me before. He is investigated for the murder and tried - then jailed. I couldnt read the verdict from the jury.<br /><br />This is a little strage but works - prison life is brushed over and he is jailed for 10ish years before a retrial caused by the book he wrote whilst inside finds him not guilty.<br /><br />At this point, he has worked out the killer is the sheriff and a showdown in a rundown hotel (which has been the "present" sections of the book) is manipulated.<br /><br />After revealing the staged suicide and teh fact the sheriff used his influence to get the Joseph as the only suspect - both men are shot - the sheriff fatally, Joseph slumbed in a chair. This is where I would have ended the book but there is a tacked on epilogue from a newspaper cutting explaining that joseph survived and went on to be a successful author.<br /><br />Everything is right in this book - the characterisation, the pace, the mood, the excitement and a damn good yarn.<br /><br />Briliiantly written. May even be book of the year.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10319563365363303276" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_197956912" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/197956912" />
    <a title="Tim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/730330-tim"><img alt="Tim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294641149p2/730330.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/197956912?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tim" href="/user/show/730330-tim">Tim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer197956912" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer786238670114541622">It's been awhile since I've encountered a narrator as tightly controlled by his author as Joseph Vaughan is in R.J. Ellory's "A Quiet Belief in Angels." There's a part of Joseph we can't quite get to, hidden by the cloak of enigma or numbness, and Ellory holds the reins relentlessly. But it's no wonder. In his story, spanning decades, Joseph is haunted by the brutal deaths of young girls in his small Georgia town. As the bodies of murdered and mutilated girls pile up in Augusta Falls and in surr</span>
  <span id="freeText786238670114541622" style="display:none">It's been awhile since I've encountered a narrator as tightly controlled by his author as Joseph Vaughan is in R.J. Ellory's "A Quiet Belief in Angels." There's a part of Joseph we can't quite get to, hidden by the cloak of enigma or numbness, and Ellory holds the reins relentlessly. But it's no wonder. In his story, spanning decades, Joseph is haunted by the brutal deaths of young girls in his small Georgia town. As the bodies of murdered and mutilated girls pile up in Augusta Falls and in surrounding counties, starting before the Second World War, Joseph organizes The Guardians, a band of his buddies determined to protect the town's young girls.<br /><br />Of course they fail. Joseph finds one of the girls, in pieces, himself. Already haunted by death — his father is gone — Joseph has a lifelong obsession with finding the murderer and with his own failings, through his mid-teen years doted on by his teacher, through his expanding relationship with her, through the apparent resolution of the culprit's identity and his mother's slipping mental grip.<br /><br />The book's back-cover description gives the impression that The Guardians play a huge role in the novel, like a gathering of Stephen King kids banding together against evil. But that element is not very prominent in "A Quiet Belief in Angels." It's a mystery story, a character study, a decades-spanning tale of Joseph's obsession. The book's opening has Joseph, as a middle-aged man, in a room with a dead man he has shot, a man he believes to be the one responsible for all the murders. Joseph's here-and-now musings keep recurring even as he details his life from boyhood to manhood and recounts the tragedies he keeps seeing/experiencing.<br /><br />In many ways, Ellory's book is a wonder, his powers of description occasionally superb. Still, there are slow spots in the tale, even if seemingly dull scenes turn out to have meaning. I found the killer's ability to commit atrocities in many communities over many years, completely unseen, to be a bit of a stretch. The story's impact lessened a bit for me as Joseph grew from boyhood, but Ellory kept satisfying twists and turns coming, and the tale did stay with me. Three stars, then, but on the very high side. I confess to not having heard of Ellory before, but he may be one who bears watching, and a look back at his earlier books may be in order. </span>
  <a data-text-id="786238670114541622" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_187175969" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/187175969" />
    <a title="Jennifer (JC-S)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/283014-jennifer-jc-s"><img alt="Jennifer (JC-S)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528085840p2/283014.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/187175969?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer (JC-S)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer (JC-S)" href="/user/show/283014-jennifer-jc-s">Jennifer (JC-S)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/283014-jennifer-jc-s?shelf=librarybooks">librarybooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer187175969" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2226903628210425592">‘In my dreams, I am a free man.’<br/><br/>One day in July 1939, when Joseph Vaughan was 12 years old, a white feather blew into his room. Joseph saw this as a sign of an angel’s visit. On the same day, his father died.<br/><br/>This angel, the Angel of Death, becomes a frequent visitor to the rural community of Augusta Falls in Georgia. And, as World War II becomes a reality in Europe, a number of young girls, classmates of Joseph, are murdered. Evil takes many different forms. Joseph wants to try to protect his co</span>
  <span id="freeText2226903628210425592" style="display:none">‘In my dreams, I am a free man.’<br /><br />One day in July 1939, when Joseph Vaughan was 12 years old, a white feather blew into his room. Joseph saw this as a sign of an angel’s visit. On the same day, his father died.<br /><br />This angel, the Angel of Death, becomes a frequent visitor to the rural community of Augusta Falls in Georgia. And, as World War II becomes a reality in Europe, a number of young girls, classmates of Joseph, are murdered. Evil takes many different forms. Joseph wants to try to protect his community, and together with his friends, forms a group called ‘The Guardians’. They are powerless to stop the killer, and the murders continue. At least ten girls have been murdered by the time Joseph reached adulthood. The nightmares that result continue to haunt him.<br /><br />‘Words are only so much use if they say something worth hearing.’<br /><br />Joseph has dreams, as well as nightmares. He dreams of being a writer, and is encouraged by his mother and his teacher. His teacher, Miss Alexandra Webber, tells him to always tell the truth as he sees it, not how others wish it to be seen. <br /><br />Joseph’s search for truth in relation to the murders is challenged by a series of horrific events in his own life. He moves to the city hoping to find peace in anonymity but still the nightmares haunt him. Joseph needs to discover the truth about the murders in order to find peace.<br />I became totally absorbed in this novel: the characters were well developed; the plot was not as straightforward as I first thought, and the language was splendid. Sometimes the pace seemed too slow, but by the end it all made sense. I think that a faster pace would have reduced the impact of the story. This is a haunting story: each character has a place in Joseph Vaughan’s life, and his life becomes very real as events unfold.<br /><br />‘At times I have believed that age is the enemy of truth.’<br /><br />Jennifer Cameron-Smith<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2226903628210425592" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_17296800" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/17296800" />
    <a title="Ali" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/804942-ali"><img alt="Ali" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1200862177p2/804942.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/17296800?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ali" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ali" href="/user/show/804942-ali">Ali</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer17296800" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14027115981015874699">Synopsis<br/>Joseph Vaughan's life has been dogged by tragedy. Growing up in the 1950s, he was at the centre of series of killings of young girls in his small rural community. The girls were taken, assaulted and left horribly mutilated. Barely a teenager himself, Joseph becomes determined to try to protect his community and classmates from the predations of the killer. Despite banding together with his friends as ' The Guardians', he was powerless to prevent more murders - and no one was ever caught.</span>
  <span id="freeText14027115981015874699" style="display:none">Synopsis<br />Joseph Vaughan's life has been dogged by tragedy. Growing up in the 1950s, he was at the centre of series of killings of young girls in his small rural community. The girls were taken, assaulted and left horribly mutilated. Barely a teenager himself, Joseph becomes determined to try to protect his community and classmates from the predations of the killer. Despite banding together with his friends as ' The Guardians', he was powerless to prevent more murders - and no one was ever caught. Only after a full ten years did the nightmare end when the one of his neighbours is found hanging from a rope, with articles from the dead girls around him. Thankfully, the killings finally ceased. But the past won't stay buried - for it seems that the real murderer still lives and is killing again. And the secret of his identity lies in Joseph's own history... <br /><br />Don't be fooled this is in no way "just a crime novel" although it does concern child murders in a small town. RJ Ellory's writing is beautiful, powerful, and at time quite haunting. This is a novel that sits right alongside such works as To Kill a Mokingbird, and Cold Blood, it's a literary novel about, life, death, love, prejudice, small town American life in the 1940's, justice, and redemption. RJ Ellory is a very gifted writer. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14027115981015874699" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_68531707" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/68531707" />
    <a title="Yassemin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2635670-yassemin"><img alt="Yassemin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602742949p2/2635670.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/68531707?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Yassemin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Yassemin" href="/user/show/2635670-yassemin">Yassemin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2635670-yassemin?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2635670-yassemin?shelf=average-nothing-special">average-nothing-special</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2635670-yassemin?shelf=british">british</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2635670-yassemin?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2635670-yassemin?shelf=crime-fiction">crime-fiction</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer68531707&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer68531707" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer407618611317644660">This book was fairly good, a good plot, fairly well written, and overall very gripping.<br/><br/>The story revolves around Joseph, a young boy living in Augusta falls in the 1930s. A series of child murders/rapes begins, spanning over decades, the murderer still lying in wait undiscovered.<br/><br/>After forming the "guardians", a group sworn to protect more of these young children from going missing and ultimately its failure to protect, as more young children are killed leads Joseph to feel blame and therefore di</span>
  <span id="freeText407618611317644660" style="display:none">This book was fairly good, a good plot, fairly well written, and overall very gripping.<br /><br />The story revolves around Joseph, a young boy living in Augusta falls in the 1930s. A series of child murders/rapes begins, spanning over decades, the murderer still lying in wait undiscovered.<br /><br />After forming the "guardians", a group sworn to protect more of these young children from going missing and ultimately its failure to protect, as more young children are killed leads Joseph to feel blame and therefore discover who is responsible for these murders, whilst experiencing lifes trials and tribulations along the way.<br /><br /><br />Its negatives for me, begin with the prose, not my kind of thing at all, it was extremely long winded at times. <br /><br />Also it took such a very long time for the story to actually progress, therefore I feel you need a lot of patience to read this book.<br /><br />The characters werent given enough dimension and felt as real as cardboard cutouts to me, I couldnt shake off my apathy towards them, I felt no real like or dislike as I didnt feel as though they were brought to life.<br /><br />The ending was anticlimatic for me and didnt really bring exceptional closure to the book for me.<br /><br />Yet, a good book, well worth reading if you have the time and patience.</span>
  <a data-text-id="407618611317644660" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
